This causes the following issue:\n\n1. **Default Behavior**: Without a quirk entry, the autodetect logic in `acpi_video_get_backlight_type()` defaults to `acpi_backlight_video` for this system\n2. **Effect on acer-wmi**: This causes the acer-wmi driver to disable its brightness capability (line 2210-2211 in acer-wmi.c) since the backlight type is not \"vendor\"\n3. **Result**: Neither the acer-wmi driver nor the generic ACPI video driver can control brightness properly\n4. **Proof**: The bug report confirms that `acpi_backlight=native` makes brightness control work perfectly with 15-16 brightness levels, proving that intel_backlight (native) is the correct driver for this model\n\n### Solution\n\nThe TravelMate 5735Z needs to be added to the `video_detect_dmi_table` with the `video_detect_force_native` callback (similar to existing entries for models like Dell Vostro V131 and Lenovo Ideapad S405), so the system uses intel_backlight by default instead of trying to use acer-wmi or the generic ACPI video driver.\n\nThe fault localization result has been written to `/workspace/fault_localization_result.json`."}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":4,"cache_creation_input_tokens":500,"cache_read_input_tokens":87535,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":500},"output_tokens":1,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"ced96264-c8e6-43dd-9280-52871686efbf","uuid":"a45fc5f0-9906-4644-a51e-8393bc4d69ef"}
